<p>Retail trade provides 9% of all jobs in India and 14% of GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-retailcomp1-a_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-retailcomp1-a-109">[109]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_for_national_retail_sales">Statistics for national retail sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Retail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Statistics for national retail sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Retail_Sales.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="915" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/US_Retail_Sales.png/290px-US_Retail_Sales.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/US_Retail_Sales.png/435px-US_Retail_Sales.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/US_Retail_Sales.png/580px-US_Retail_Sales.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Retail_Sales.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Monthly Retail Sales, 1992–2010</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Retail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Retail_Federation" title="National Retail Federation">National Retail Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kantar_Group" title="Kantar Group">Kantar</a> annually rank the nation's top retailers according to sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The National Retail Federation also separately ranks the 100 fastest-growing U.S. retailers based on increases in domestic sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1951, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Census_Bureau" title="U.S. Census Bureau">U.S. Census Bureau</a> has published the Retail Sales report every month. It is a measure of <a href="/wiki/Consumer_spending" title="Consumer spending">consumer spending</a>, an important indicator of the US <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>. Retail firms provide data on the dollar value of their retail sales and inventories. A <a href="/wiki/Sampling_(statistics)" title="Sampling (statistics)">sample</a> of 12,000 firms is included in the final <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statistical_survey" title="Statistical survey">survey</a> and 5,000 in the advanced one. The advanced estimated data is based on a subsample from the US CB complete retail &amp; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Food_service" title="Food service">food services</a> sample.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>Retail is the largest private-sector employer in the United States, supporting 52 million working Americans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3102" data-file-width="2068" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg/170px-Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg/255px-Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg/340px-Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zuerich_Migroshochhaus_5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The two largest supermarkets chains in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Migros" title="Migros">Migros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coop_(Switzerland)" title="Coop (Switzerland)">Coop</a>, are cooperatives.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_Europe">Central Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Retail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Central Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 2011, the grocery market in six countries of <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a> was worth nearly €107bn, 2.8% more than the previous year when expressed in local currencies. The increase was generated foremost by the discount stores and supermarket segments, and was driven by the skyrocketing prices of foodstuffs. This information is based on the latest PMR report entitled Grocery retail in Central Europe 2012<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-http://www.pmrpublications.com/product/Grocery-retail-Central-Europe-2012_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-http://www.pmrpublications.com/product/Grocery-retail-Central-Europe-2012-116">[116]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World">World</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Retail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: World">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station,_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="805" data-file-width="805" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station%2C_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG/170px-016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station%2C_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station%2C_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG/255px-016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station%2C_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station%2C_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG/340px-016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station%2C_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:016_Coca-Cola_vending_machine_at_Kyoto_Station,_Japan_-_%E3%82%B3%E3%82%AB%E3%82%B3%E3%83%BC%E3%83%A9_%E8%87%AA%E5%8B%95%E8%B2%A9%E5%A3%B2%E6%A9%9F.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> has the largest number of vending machines per capita.</div></div></div>
<p>National accounts show a combined total of retail and wholesale trade, with hotels and restaurants. in 2012 the sector provides over a fifth of GDP in tourist-oriented island economies, as well as in other major countries such as Brazil, Pakistan, Russia, and Spain. In all four of the latter countries, this fraction is an increase over 1970, but there are other countries where the sector has declined since 1970, sometimes in absolute terms, where other sectors have replaced its role in the economy. In the United States the sector has declined from 19% of GDP to 14%, though it has risen in absolute terms from $4,500 to $7,400 per capita per year. In China the sector has grown from 7.3% to 11.5%, and in India even more, from 8.4% to 18.7%. Emarketer predicts China will have the largest retail market in the world in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> became the largest retail market in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.emarketer.com_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.emarketer.com-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Influential thinkers in sales and retail:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dale_Carnegie" title="Dale Carnegie">Dale Carnegie</a>: author and lecturer; proponent of salesmanship, public speaking and self-improvement</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/E._St._Elmo_Lewis" title="E. St. Elmo Lewis">E. St. Elmo Lewis</a>: salesmen for NCR and developer of the <a href="/wiki/AIDA_(marketing)" title="AIDA (marketing)">AIDA model of selling</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/William_Thomas_Rawleigh" title="William Thomas Rawleigh">William Thomas Rawleigh</a>: founder of Rawleigh's company with one of the largest travelling sales teams in the United States</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Gordon_Selfridge" title="Harry Gordon Selfridge">Harry Gordon Selfridge</a>: founder of UK Selfridges; redefined shopping away from essential errand to a pleasurable activity; was noted for introducing a touch of theatre and celebrity appearances to department stores; also wrote the book, <i>The Romance of Commerce</i> published in 1918.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Walter_Dill_Scott" title="Walter Dill Scott">Walter Dill Scott</a>: psychologist and author; wrote a number of books on the psychology of selling in the early twentieth century</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Watson" title="Thomas J. Watson">Thomas J. Watson</a>: salesman at NCR and CEO of IBM; often described as the "greatest American salesman"</li></ul>

Holman and Michael R. Solomon (eds.), Provo, UT: Association for Consumer Research, 1991, pp. 426–27</li>
<li>Hollander, S.C., "Who and What are Important in Retailing and Marketing History: A Basis for Discussion", in S.C. Hollander and R. Savitt (eds.) <i>First North American Workshop on Historical Research in Marketing</i>, Lansing, MI: Michigan State University, 1983, pp. 35–40.</li>
